# Outlook on the Web Essential Training

> Follow along with Gini von Courter as she takes you on a tour of the new Outlook on the web, the browser version of the popular email and calendar app from Microsoft. Gini shows how to send, receive, and manage email, as well as how to organize, flag, and pin your messages. Discover how to work with the calendar features in Outlook on the web, including how to create repeating appointments, reques

> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889) | 3h 5m | 23K learners
> [Jump to Path Context ↓](#path-context)

- **6. 5. Work with Meetings and Bookings** (6 videos)

### 1. Introduction

#### Manage your email and calendar with Outlook on the web

>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/manage-your-email-and-calendar-with-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=4)** With Outlook on the web, you don't need to install anything.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/manage-your-email-and-calendar-with-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=7)** Simply open a browser and jump right in.

#### What Outlook on the web is and isn't
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/what-outlook-on-the-web-is-and-isn-t?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/what-outlook-on-the-web-is-and-isn-t?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] The infrastructure for email is modeled on a postal system.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/what-outlook-on-the-web-is-and-isn-t?u=76281980&t=5)** The Post Office uses physical post office buildings and physical mailboxes while email systems use email servers and client mailboxes.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/what-outlook-on-the-web-is-and-isn-t?u=76281980&t=14)** The server, which in our case is Microsoft Exchange Server, behaves just like the Post Office.
>
> **[0:20](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/what-outlook-on-the-web-is-and-isn-t?u=76281980&t=20)** Exchange Server is where mail is received and sorted, where it's stored and where it's delivered from.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/what-outlook-on-the-web-is-and-isn-t?u=76281980&t=27)** Email clients operate like mailboxes, where you can both receive and send email, and the most popular client for Exchange Server is a program called Outlook.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/what-outlook-on-the-web-is-and-isn-t?u=76281980&t=38)** Outlook is full-featured desktop software that needs to be installed on your local Windows machine.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/what-outlook-on-the-web-is-and-isn-t?u=76281980&t=43)** The desktop version of Outlook looks like something we spent money on because we did.
>
> **[0:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/what-outlook-on-the-web-is-and-isn-t?u=76281980&t=48)** It's shiny, it's fabulous, and it's full featured, but it's not the only client for Exchange Server, not by any means.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/what-outlook-on-the-web-is-and-isn-t?u=76281980&t=56)** At this point, the name Outlook is used to describe a number of different email clients that run on different devices.
>
> **[1:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/what-outlook-on-the-web-is-and-isn-t?u=76281980&t=64)** In some ways, Outlook is more of a brand than a product.
>
> **[1:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/what-outlook-on-the-web-is-and-isn-t?u=76281980&t=67)** Outlook for Mac is the Mac version of Outlook, and it is installed on a Mac just like Outlook is installed on Windows PCs.
>
> **[1:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/what-outlook-on-the-web-is-and-isn-t?u=76281980&t=76)** Outlook on the web is a powerful universal client for Exchange Server.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/what-outlook-on-the-web-is-and-isn-t?u=76281980&t=82)** No matter where in the world I am, I can use Outlook on the web to send and receive email, check my calendar, update my tasks, or find information about contacts.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/what-outlook-on-the-web-is-and-isn-t?u=76281980&t=91)** Outlook on the web runs in a number of browsers, and this course is all about Outlook on the web.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/what-outlook-on-the-web-is-and-isn-t?u=76281980&t=98)** But wait, there's more.
>
> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/what-outlook-on-the-web-is-and-isn-t?u=76281980&t=99)** [Outlook.com](https://Outlook.com) is a free, web-based email account, which used to be called Hotmail.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/what-outlook-on-the-web-is-and-isn-t?u=76281980&t=106)** The app for [Outlook.com](https://Outlook.com) is similar to Outlook on the web, so if your email address ends in [hotmail.com](https://hotmail.com), [live.com](https://live.com), [msn.com](https://msn.com), or [outlook.com](https://outlook.com), some of the things that you would learn in this course will be useful to you.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/what-outlook-on-the-web-is-and-isn-t?u=76281980&t=123)** There are also Outlook mobile apps, which run on phones and tablets, and you can easily download these free apps in the same place that you would download other apps for your device.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/what-outlook-on-the-web-is-and-isn-t?u=76281980&t=133)** For a number of years, Microsoft Windows has included separate Mail, Calendar, and People apps so that users could have access to things like mail and calendar without purchasing other software, but they're very simple apps.
>
> **[2:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/what-outlook-on-the-web-is-and-isn-t?u=76281980&t=149)** Beginning in 2024, when you get a new PC running Windows 11, or in some cases when you update to Windows 11, it won't include these separate apps.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/what-outlook-on-the-web-is-and-isn-t?u=76281980&t=161)** Instead, it will include a new Outlook product called New Outlook for Windows 11, and you'll be able to still download the Mail, Calendar and People apps, but only till the end of 2024.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/what-outlook-on-the-web-is-and-isn-t?u=76281980&t=176)** This course focuses on Outlook on the web.
>
> **[2:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/what-outlook-on-the-web-is-and-isn-t?u=76281980&t=179)** You don't need to have anything installed on your local computer to use Outlook on the web, and it is a powerful universal application that has quickly become a go-to product for Outlook power users.
>
> **[3:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/what-outlook-on-the-web-is-and-isn-t?u=76281980&t=195)** Let's continue.

### 2. 1. Get Started with Outlook on the Web

#### Sign in to Outlook on the web
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/sign-in-to-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/sign-in-to-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] There are two easy ways to sign in to Outlook on the web.
>
> **[0:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/sign-in-to-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=4)** If you're running another application, like Microsoft Teams or SharePoint, that includes the app launcher, also called the waffle, in the upper left-hand corner, you can click the waffle and choose Outlook.
>
> **[0:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/sign-in-to-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=16)** And when you do, it will automatically load Outlook on the web.
>
> **[0:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/sign-in-to-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=22)** If you're not already logged in to Outlook on the web, then what you can do is open a browser and type outlook.[office.com](https://office.com) and press Enter.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/sign-in-to-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=37)** If you don't already have an account and you're logging in for the first time, go to outlook.[office.com](https://office.com), and you'll be prompted to log in.
>
> **[0:49](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/sign-in-to-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=49)** So log in with your work or school account.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/sign-in-to-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=53)** You'll need to enter your email address and enter a password for your work or school account, so this is a first-time login, and then choose Sign In.
>
> **[1:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/sign-in-to-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=62)** So these are really your two options: use the app launcher or go to outlook.[office.com](https://office.com) and log in.
>
> **[1:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/sign-in-to-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=73)** At this point, you may say, "I'd like to learn this, but I don't have a work or school account already connected to Microsoft Exchange Server."
>
> **[1:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/sign-in-to-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=81)** If that's the case, then you can still follow along with me by getting a free trial of Microsoft Office.
>
> **[1:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/sign-in-to-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=91)** So go to a browser, type Microsoft Office Free Trial,
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/sign-in-to-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=101)** and scroll down to the first entry from Microsoft, "Free Trial: Try Microsoft 365 for a Month."
>
> **[1:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/sign-in-to-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=111)** Click here, and you can start a free one-month trial, which will include access to not just Outlook, but Word, Excel, and all of the other applications.
>
> **[2:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/sign-in-to-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=124)** If you need to get a free trial, this is a good time to do that.
>
> **[2:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/sign-in-to-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=127)** And sign into Outlook.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/sign-in-to-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=133)** And I will see you in Outlook in the next movie.

#### Navigate in Outlook on the web
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/navigate-in-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/navigate-in-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Let's take a quick tour of Outlook on the web.
>
> **[0:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/navigate-in-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=3)** In the upper left hand corner, we have the Microsoft 365 app launcher or the waffle.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/navigate-in-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=8)** And if we drop directly below that, we have the Outlook navigation bar with the core Outlook applications listed at the top, Email, Calendar, and People.
>
> **[0:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/navigate-in-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=21)** These three buttons fire up those applications within Outlook.
>
> **[0:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/navigate-in-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=25)** By default, when Outlook on the web loads, it loads Email.
>
> **[0:30](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/navigate-in-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=30)** Next I have the button displayed for Microsoft 365 groups.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/navigate-in-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=34)** You'd click this icon to view your active groups and discover new groups.
>
> **[0:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/navigate-in-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=38)** The To Do icon launches the To Do app.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/navigate-in-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=42)** But for any of these, if you right click, you can choose to display that app in a new tab rather than switching the current browser tab to that application.
>
> **[0:51](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/navigate-in-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=51)** And this is a good time to point out that you can also unpin applications from this left hand Outlook navigation if you don't want, for example, to have an icon for To Do or for Groups.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/navigate-in-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=63)** The only two apps you can't unpin, Mail or the Calendar apps.
>
> **[1:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/navigate-in-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=70)** Below To Do, which operates like a task list, we have a link to OneDrive and then other apps, which allows you to go directly to apps like Excel, Word, and PowerPoint, or to add other apps to your Outlook nav bar here on the left hand side.
>
> **[1:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/navigate-in-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=85)** To the right of the Outlook navigation bar is the navigation pane for whatever app is being displayed.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/navigate-in-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=92)** So while I'm in my inbox, the navigation pane that I see includes folders, favorites, groups, and so on.
>
> **[1:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/navigate-in-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=100)** If I switch to Calendar, my navigation pane in the calendar displays a date navigator at the top, my calendar's down below, and I can add other calendars, for example.
>
> **[1:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/navigate-in-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=113)** I'm going to switch back to email.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/navigate-in-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=114)** And by the way, if you want to hide this navigation pane in any of the apps, these three lines at the top to the left of Home and to the right of the Outlook navigation bar, will display or hide this navigation pane.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/navigate-in-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=130)** To the right of the navigation pane, most of the apps have what's called an information viewer that lists individual items so that you can scroll and go to a specific email, for example.
>
> **[2:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/navigate-in-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=141)** To the right then of the information viewer, we have the preview pane that is letting us view and take action on whatever item we have displayed in the information viewer.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/navigate-in-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=153)** Each app has its own ribbon at the top.
>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/navigate-in-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=156)** This is a ribbon that is customizable, commands that aren't included on this very compact ribbon, you get to by clicking the more button, and at the very bottom you'll see that you could indeed customize the ribbon in all of the applications.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/navigate-in-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=170)** Let's swing back up here to the title bar and finish off our basic navigation here.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/navigate-in-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=176)** This is a search box that allows us to search and filter within Outlook.
>
> **[3:02](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/navigate-in-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=182)** To the right of search, there's a button that will connect you to Teams so that you can chat directly from Outlook in Teams.
>
> **[3:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/navigate-in-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=191)** To the right of our chat button is a connection to our OneNote feed, so you can search in OneNote and also post new items in OneNote.
>
> **[3:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/navigate-in-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=199)** The third icon is for My Day, a combination of calendar and tasks.
>
> **[3:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/navigate-in-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=204)** To the right of that is notifications, and if this is highlighted or has a number next to it, click on it to see what you need to be notified about.
>
> **[3:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/navigate-in-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=212)** To the right of notifications, the gear button for settings, this is where we will set all of our options in Outlook, whether it's for Mail, Calendar, People, or our general options.
>
> **[3:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/navigate-in-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=226)** And then there's a Tips button.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/navigate-in-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=228)** Now, it isn't always here, it's here if you have tips you haven't viewed yet.
>
> **[3:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/navigate-in-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=233)** So if it's ever not there, don't worry about it, but there are all kinds of tips available, including what's coming soon, updates that are available, what's new, and so on, and it just opens a flyout pane from the right so that you can learn a little more about what's going on with Outlook.
>
> **[4:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/navigate-in-outlook-on-the-web?u=76281980&t=248)** Finally, in the upper right hand corner, your initials or image is a button that opens your account manager so that you can view your account, open another mailbox, switch between accounts, and most importantly, if you are working on a public computer, sign out before you close the browser, right here.

### 3. 2. Compose and Send Messages

#### Create a new message
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-new-message?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-new-message?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] To create a new email message, make sure you are in the mail app in Outlook on the Web and click the New Mail button and a new message form will open up in the preview pane on the right.
>
> **[0:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-new-message?u=76281980&t=13)** There are three ways that I can add someone's email address and up to three places that I can put email addresses: To, Cc, and Bcc.
>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-new-message?u=76281980&t=24)** I use To when I want whoever I send this message to not just to read it, but to reply to me.
>
> **[0:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-new-message?u=76281980&t=32)** And when I click in the To box, notice that I have some suggested contacts.
>
> **[0:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-new-message?u=76281980&t=36)** These are people that I have emailed either recently or frequently.
>
> **[0:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-new-message?u=76281980&t=42)** And if there was one of these that I didn't want to show up on the list, then I could simply point to them, hover and click the X to remove them from the list.
>
> **[0:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-new-message?u=76281980&t=53)** It's not like I have room for 50 contacts here, so if one of these isn't one that I use frequently, I should just remove it from my suggestions.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-new-message?u=76281980&t=63)** But when I click in To, I'm going to send an email to Charles and I can just click there in To.
>
> **[1:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-new-message?u=76281980&t=68)** What if I didn't want Charles to reply to me?
>
> **[1:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-new-message?u=76281980&t=74)** I just wanted him to read something.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-new-message?u=76281980&t=75)** Well, then I would put Charles in Cc because Cc says read, but you don't need to get back with me.
>
> **[1:22](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-new-message?u=76281980&t=82)** The third option is Bcc, and there's not a text box for it by default, but if you click Bcc, a third text box will open.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-new-message?u=76281980&t=89)** And I want to talk to you about the two appropriate uses of Bcc or what used to be called blind courtesy copy.
>
> **[1:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-new-message?u=76281980&t=97)** So this is To, Courtesy Copy, and Blind Courtesy Copy.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-new-message?u=76281980&t=101)** The first appropriate use is if you are sending the same email to a group of people, for example, 30 people, and you don't want them to see each other's email addresses, then you would simply invite them all by adding them to this Bcc line.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-new-message?u=76281980&t=117)** So Charles and Griffin and Reggie will all get this email, but none of them will know that the other received it.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-new-message?u=76281980&t=128)** So it's really for privacy reasons because they don't see the other people's emails.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-new-message?u=76281980&t=133)** Another use of this is I'm sending something to Charles, but I want to make sure that Reggie, who is my administrative professional, follows up on this, but Charles doesn't need to know I'm going to have Reggie do this, so I'm going to drop Reggie in as a Bcc because Reggie will read it and being the smart person that they are will say, "Oh, okay, this is something Gini needs me to follow up on."
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-new-message?u=76281980&t=157)** So those are the two good ethical uses of Bcc.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-new-message?u=76281980&t=161)** A less good use of Bcc, and one I advise you not to use, is when you're writing to someone, for example, if I'm writing to Griffin and I'm complaining to Griffin about something they did, but I want to sneakily copy in Griffin's supervisor on this, that's not a good use of Bcc.
>
> **[3:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-new-message?u=76281980&t=180)** It's not transparent. It's not kind.
>
> **[3:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-new-message?u=76281980&t=183)** And often it's problematic because if Charles were to reply to all, Griffin would then see the reply and actually know that Charles had been copied on this, in a way that wasn't transparent.
>
> **[3:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-new-message?u=76281980&t=197)** So two good ways to Bcc: one for a group of people for privacy and the other is to give an assignment to someone that it's not important to the recipient to know that you're doing that.
>
> **[3:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-new-message?u=76281980&t=209)** So you've already seen one way that I can add people, which is simply to choose them from the list.
>
> **[3:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-new-message?u=76281980&t=214)** A second way I can do it is to begin typing their information and notice that I'm getting a new list of suggestions based on people whose names include the letters that I am typing.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-new-message?u=76281980&t=228)** And if one of these is just plain wrong, you can delete it and it will never then appear again as a suggestion.
>
> **[3:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-new-message?u=76281980&t=237)** Notice, gone.
>
> **[3:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-new-message?u=76281980&t=239)** The third way that I can add someone to this list is to type their email address in full.
>
> **[4:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-new-message?u=76281980&t=247)** And that's what I need to do for someone who's not in my contact list, not in any address book that is connected to Microsoft Outlook.
>
> **[4:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-new-message?u=76281980&t=255)** So if I wanted to send something to someone specific who wasn't in my address book, then I would begin typing their entire email address and I would have to continue typing until I had it fully typed.
>
> **[4:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-new-message?u=76281980&t=272)** Once I'm done adding the people that I want to send this email to, then I add a subject and I enter that right here.
>
> **[4:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-new-message?u=76281980&t=279)** And in terms of subject, you want a good subject.
>
> **[4:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-new-message?u=76281980&t=282)** You don't want something that simply says, "Help" or "For your information," make it a subject about the content of the email.
>
> **[4:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-new-message?u=76281980&t=290)** So this is about the Microsoft 365 new features.
>
> **[4:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-new-message?u=76281980&t=296)** Once I get below the subject, I can either click or I can tab down to the body of my email.
>
> **[5:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-new-message?u=76281980&t=303)** And once I get into the body, all of these other buttons on my ribbon come to life.
>
> **[5:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-new-message?u=76281980&t=308)** I don't have formatting buttons available to me in the text boxes for things like subject or recipients, but here I have access to the entire font list.

#### Add a loop component to a message
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/add-a-loop-component-to-a-message?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/add-a-loop-component-to-a-message?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Trainer] Loop components which appear on our ribbon are portable content collaboration spaces, like a smaller version of a shared document.
>
> **[0:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/add-a-loop-component-to-a-message?u=76281980&t=10)** Loop components are automatically stored in your OneDrive, and you can embed a loop component in an email.
>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/add-a-loop-component-to-a-message?u=76281980&t=17)** You can also embed a loop component in a calendar event, like a meeting or an appointment.
>

#### Add a scheduling poll to a message
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/add-a-scheduling-poll-to-a-message?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/add-a-scheduling-poll-to-a-message?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] Another reason we might need to poll colleagues is to learn about their availability.
>
> **[0:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/add-a-scheduling-poll-to-a-message?u=76281980&t=7)** So I'm going to create a new message and show you another type of poll that we can insert called a scheduling poll.
>

### 4. 3. Receive and Manage Messages

#### Use the Focused Inbox
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/use-the-focused-inbox?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/use-the-focused-inbox?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] We've been doing a deeper dive into what we can do with individual messages, but I want to back out a bit so that we can look at the inbox as a whole.
>
> **[0:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/use-the-focused-inbox?u=76281980&t=8)** The messages that I currently see in the Information Viewer are not the only messages that I've received recently, and that's because Microsoft Outlook on the web uses a Focused inbox.
>
> **[0:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/use-the-focused-inbox?u=76281980&t=18)** It separates your incoming messages onto two different tabs, Focused and Other, or another way to think about it, Important and Other.
>
> **[0:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/use-the-focused-inbox?u=76281980&t=27)** On the Focused tab, you'll see items that were sent specifically to you, items that were sent by individuals rather than organizations, messages that have been forwarded to you.
>
> **[0:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/use-the-focused-inbox?u=76281980&t=37)** Wherever the message comes from, the algorithm built into Outlook believes that you might want to see them first.
>
> **[0:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/use-the-focused-inbox?u=76281980&t=43)** And so, they are placed on the Focused tab.
>
> **[0:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/use-the-focused-inbox?u=76281980&t=45)** Everything else, messages that come from organizations, messages that appear to be newsletters, messages sent to hundreds of people, those end up on the Other tab.
>
> **[0:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/use-the-focused-inbox?u=76281980&t=54)** For this two-tab system to work well for you, you need to adjust it.
>
> **[0:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/use-the-focused-inbox?u=76281980&t=59)** And you do that as you're reviewing messages.
>
> **[1:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/use-the-focused-inbox?u=76281980&t=61)** For example, if you're looking at the Focused inbox and you find a message from someone and you think, "Why is this here? That isn't that important to me."
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/use-the-focused-inbox?u=76281980&t=69)** And if that's the case, you can right click on the message, you can choose Move, and then choose Always move to other inbox.
>
> **[1:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/use-the-focused-inbox?u=76281980&t=79)** By doing that, I'm saying, send this message and every other message from this sender over to the Other tab.
>
> **[1:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/use-the-focused-inbox?u=76281980&t=86)** It's less important to me.
>
> **[1:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/use-the-focused-inbox?u=76281980&t=89)** When I do that, I'm prompted to say, "Yep, that's what I want to do."
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/use-the-focused-inbox?u=76281980&t=92)** You click Okay.
>
> **[1:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/use-the-focused-inbox?u=76281980&t=93)** And that message and future messages from the same sender go to the Other tab.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/use-the-focused-inbox?u=76281980&t=98)** And when I start my day, I'm going to work the Focused tab first.
>
> **[1:42](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/use-the-focused-inbox?u=76281980&t=102)** That's the point of this.
>
> **[1:43](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/use-the-focused-inbox?u=76281980&t=103)** And after I've worked through my new messages on Focused, I'm going to switch to the Other tab and look at messages there.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/use-the-focused-inbox?u=76281980&t=110)** Now, in the same way, I might see a message and go, "Wow, I can't believe that this went to the Other tab.
>
> **[1:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/use-the-focused-inbox?u=76281980&t=116)** I really want to make sure that I see these messages in the future."
>
> **[2:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/use-the-focused-inbox?u=76281980&t=120)** And if that's the case, you do exactly the same thing.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/use-the-focused-inbox?u=76281980&t=123)** You right click on a message that is from the sender that you would like to have appear on the Focused tab.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/use-the-focused-inbox?u=76281980&t=130)** Choose Move, Always move to Focused inbox.
>
> **[2:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/use-the-focused-inbox?u=76281980&t=133)** Now, a distinction between Always move and Move is Move moves one message, the message that is selected right now, or if you'd selected five messages, you could send five.
>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/use-the-focused-inbox?u=76281980&t=144)** Always move is not just all the messages on the Other tab now, but all the messages that will come into the inbox in the future.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/use-the-focused-inbox?u=76281980&t=152)** So, make whatever choice you want to make.
>
> **[2:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/use-the-focused-inbox?u=76281980&t=154)** Validate it by clicking Okay.
>
> **[2:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/use-the-focused-inbox?u=76281980&t=156)** And you've now changed the rules for how Outlook on the web is sorting your messages into these two tabs.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/use-the-focused-inbox?u=76281980&t=164)** The more effort you put into tuning this system, the better it's going to work for you.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/use-the-focused-inbox?u=76281980&t=170)** So, when you're working with Outlook on the web early on, that's a good time to be more aggressive with telling Outlook on the web what belongs on Other and what belongs on Focused.
>
> **[3:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/use-the-focused-inbox?u=76281980&t=180)** As time goes on, you'll have to do less of that because each tweak you make is being instructive to Outlook on the web about how you want to work, what you think is important and belongs on Focused.
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/use-the-focused-inbox?u=76281980&t=193)** What you think is less important that should be placed on the Other tab.

> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/print-a-message?u=76281980&t=5)** So if I want to print just a message, I have two places that I can easily do that.
>

>
> **[0:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/print-a-message?u=76281980&t=31)** So both of these More Actions toolbars give you a print command.

> **[5:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-and-manage-subfolders?u=76281980&t=356)** You want to keep things there that are currently cooking.

> **[6:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-and-manage-subfolders?u=76281980&t=371)** My advice to you is to create folders as you need them, but with an extra question.

>
> **[6:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-and-manage-subfolders?u=76281980&t=404)** That intermediate level is simply allowing you to more easily search, because if I have five projects folders, and I want to search all of them, I can select Projects, even if there's nothing in it, and search, because search is allowing me to search for this folder and automatically, all of its sub folders.
>
> **[7:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-and-manage-subfolders?u=76281980&t=423)** If you find that you have a folder you don't use, for heaven's sakes, get rid of it.

> **[7:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-and-manage-subfolders?u=76281980&t=427)** Right click on it and delete the folder.

> **[7:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-and-manage-subfolders?u=76281980&t=431)** If there are items in it, they will also be deleted.

> **[7:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-and-manage-subfolders?u=76281980&t=433)** If you don't want the items gone, move them first to the appropriate folder, the inbox or elsewhere.

> **[1:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/archive-or-sweep-messages?u=76281980&t=99)** Or I can make it time-based and say, as soon as it's been in my inbox for more than 10 days, sweep it out of here.
>
> **[1:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/archive-or-sweep-messages?u=76281980&t=107)** So, four options.
>
> **[1:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/archive-or-sweep-messages?u=76281980&t=108)** Move them all, but only the messages I've already received.
>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/archive-or-sweep-messages?u=76281980&t=114)** The second option, move all the messages I have in the inbox and any that come in the future.
>
> **[2:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/archive-or-sweep-messages?u=76281980&t=121)** Third option, keep just one and the rest of them go.
>
> **[2:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/archive-or-sweep-messages?u=76281980&t=125)** And the fourth option, if it's been hanging around for 10 days or more, move it.
>
> **[2:10](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/archive-or-sweep-messages?u=76281980&t=130)** This is a way to keep your inbox lean because if I have a message that's been hanging around in my inbox for more than 10 days and I haven't read it yet, I'm probably saving it for a time that I have a little bit of slack in my work and I'm going to then go review an entire folder of messages.
>
> **[2:26](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/archive-or-sweep-messages?u=76281980&t=146)** So I will say, always keep the latest message and move the rest from the inbox.
>
> **[2:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/archive-or-sweep-messages?u=76281980&t=151)** And these, all of these options, but the first, apply to current and future messages.
>
> **[2:37](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/archive-or-sweep-messages?u=76281980&t=157)** Click Okay, Sweep. Success.
>
> **[2:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/archive-or-sweep-messages?u=76281980&t=160)** You'll only see the latest message from the sender you specified and we're working on cleaning up your inbox.
>
> **[2:45](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/archive-or-sweep-messages?u=76281980&t=165)** Then it says View Rules, because doing this, you actually created a rule.
>
> **[2:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/archive-or-sweep-messages?u=76281980&t=170)** Creating and managing rules from scratch other than with Sweep or Archive are beyond the scope of this course.
>
> **[2:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/archive-or-sweep-messages?u=76281980&t=176)** But take a look at Outlook Efficient Email Management in the LinkedIn Learning Library if you'd like to know more about how to work with rules.
>
> **[3:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/archive-or-sweep-messages?u=76281980&t=183)** So, this is one way to do this.
>
> **[3:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/archive-or-sweep-messages?u=76281980&t=184)** I can sweep them someplace else.
>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/archive-or-sweep-messages?u=76281980&t=187)** There's another option for dealing with messages that I'm done with.
>
> **[3:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/archive-or-sweep-messages?u=76281980&t=191)** I can move them to an archive.
>
> **[3:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/archive-or-sweep-messages?u=76281980&t=193)** I don't need to do that using the move dropdown.
>
> **[3:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/archive-or-sweep-messages?u=76281980&t=195)** There's an archive button right here.
>
> **[3:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/archive-or-sweep-messages?u=76281980&t=198)** Why would I archive messages?
>
> **[3:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/archive-or-sweep-messages?u=76281980&t=199)** Because I don't want them in my inbox.
>
> **[3:21](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/archive-or-sweep-messages?u=76281980&t=201)** I don't want them in sub-folders in my inbox, perhaps because my organization makes me try to keep my inbox really small.
>
> **[3:29](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/archive-or-sweep-messages?u=76281980&t=209)** But when I search, I still want to be able to find them.
>
> **[3:31](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/archive-or-sweep-messages?u=76281980&t=211)** Archiving literally puts them in a separate storage, a separate folder.

>
> **[3:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/archive-or-sweep-messages?u=76281980&t=227)** If you primarily use Outlook on the web, that might be a reason to use Outlook on your desktop would be to set up an archive structure for all of your different folders.
>
> **[3:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/archive-or-sweep-messages?u=76281980&t=236)** The inbox, but your sub-folders as well.
>
> **[3:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/archive-or-sweep-messages?u=76281980&t=239)** Tools like Sweep and Archive give you an opportunity to be introspective about your work habits.
>
> **[4:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/archive-or-sweep-messages?u=76281980&t=245)** If you return over and over again to messages that you're not going to do anything with, then set up some sweep rules or archive them if you're required to keep them, and get them out of your way.

> **[4:16](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/archive-or-sweep-messages?u=76281980&t=256)** Judicious use of Sweep and Archive will help you maintain an inbox that's easier to manage and easier to work in.

### 5. 4. Use the Calendar

#### Navigate in the Calendar app
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/navigate-in-the-calendar-app?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>

> **[2:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-appointment?u=76281980&t=135)** If that's not a good time for you, choose another time that's the same.
>
> **[2:19](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-appointment?u=76281980&t=139)** But I know that something I'm going to do in that part of the year when there's not much to do except hold parties and everybody's out of the office, I'm going to redo my repeating appointments for the following year.
>
> **[2:33](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-appointment?u=76281980&t=153)** When you're all done, click Save to save the repeating and then Save again.
>
> **[2:40](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-appointment?u=76281980&t=160)** So here's this Friday, I'm going to switch to a month view.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-appointment?u=76281980&t=164)** And you will notice that every other Friday as I work down my calendar every two weeks, there's that appointment, that repeating appointment.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-appointment?u=76281980&t=175)** If you want to get rid of a repeating appointment and delete it, you have a choice.
>
> **[3:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-appointment?u=76281980&t=180)** The choice says, I want to get rid of just one, just this one for example.
>
> **[3:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-appointment?u=76281980&t=185)** I want to get rid of this one and all of them that follow.
>
> **[3:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-appointment?u=76281980&t=188)** So for whatever reason, I'm not going to do it anymore.
>
> **[3:11](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-appointment?u=76281980&t=191)** Maybe we have a new automated system and I don't need to do a time sheet or just get rid of them and pretend that they never happened.
>
> **[3:18](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-appointment?u=76281980&t=198)** Typically, that's only a good choice if none of those appointments have actually happened.
>
> **[3:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-appointment?u=76281980&t=203)** One more thought.
>
> **[3:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-appointment?u=76281980&t=205)** It might be that there are some times that I know I'm going to be out of the office, so I know, for example, that I will not be available this last week in April, and I need to turn this time sheet in a couple days early, I can just take that appointment and move it just like that.
>
> **[3:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-appointment?u=76281980&t=221)** This appointment is still part of that series, but it breaks the pattern and so the little repeat symbol has a line through it.
>
> **[3:48](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-appointment?u=76281980&t=228)** If I later go back and edit this to change anything about the repeat, the day it happens and the duration, this one will snap back to where it was originally.
>
> **[3:59](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-appointment?u=76281980&t=239)** But this is a way to be able to move or delete a particular appointment in a series of repeating appointments.

>
> **[4:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/respond-to-a-meeting-invitation?u=76281980&t=247)** And if I think it might be a couple days until Charles changes this meeting, I'm actually going to take a second and I'm going to put in "hold for HR IT meeting change," because it's embarrassing if I ask Charles to change the meeting and then I schedule something else to start at 2:00.
>
> **[4:27](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/respond-to-a-meeting-invitation?u=76281980&t=267)** So I'm going to just drop that into my calendar so that I have it, because until Charles accepts that change, this is still a meeting from noon to 2:00, even though I've said it's not particularly going to work for me.
>
> **[4:39](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/respond-to-a-meeting-invitation?u=76281980&t=279)** So the meeting doesn't go away, it's still in my inbox.
>
> **[4:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/respond-to-a-meeting-invitation?u=76281980&t=284)** When I accept a meeting, it's removed from my inbox.
>
> **[4:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/respond-to-a-meeting-invitation?u=76281980&t=287)** When I decline a meeting, it is deleted from my inbox and from my calendar.
>
> **[4:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/respond-to-a-meeting-invitation?u=76281980&t=293)** But if I say maybe or I propose a new time, I'm going to be hanging onto these emails until this conversation has ended.
>
> **[5:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/respond-to-a-meeting-invitation?u=76281980&t=300)** So really, five different ways I can respond to a meeting.
>
> **[5:04](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/respond-to-a-meeting-invitation?u=76281980&t=304)** Yes, no, maybe, set a new time, please, because I can't come otherwise, and set a new time, please because it's more convenient for me.
>
> **[5:13](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/respond-to-a-meeting-invitation?u=76281980&t=313)** Choose whichever one of those is going to work for you, and you'll see those changes appropriately reflected in your calendar.

#### Create a repeating meeting
> [LinkedIn Learning](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-meeting?u=76281980)

> [!transcript]- Transcript
>
> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-meeting?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Narrator] Just as you can create repeating appointments, you can create repeating meetings.
>
> **[0:05](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-meeting?u=76281980&t=5)** So I'm going to set up a new meeting that is going to be a meeting that happens once a month for an hour.
>
> **[0:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-meeting?u=76281980&t=14)** And this is the Monthly Budget Dive, is what it gets called.
>

>
> **[0:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-meeting?u=76281980&t=24)** So I'm going to click More options and change this from Don't repeat to Monthly on the third Tuesday every month.
>
> **[0:34](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-meeting?u=76281980&t=34)** And I'm going to change the end date to be the end of the year, because that's my practice, to reset all of these at the end of the calendar year.
>
> **[0:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-meeting?u=76281980&t=44)** And who am I going to invite?
>
> **[0:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-meeting?u=76281980&t=46)** Let me say at this point that if I were going to make a number of exceptions to this, if, for example, most of these meetings are going to happen on the third Tuesday.
>
> **[0:56](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-meeting?u=76281980&t=56)** But if the third Tuesday is the day after a holiday, which is going to happen three times this year, we're going to move it by a week.
>
> **[1:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-meeting?u=76281980&t=63)** If I had a number of those, I would actually change those meetings first before I invited anyone.
>
> **[1:09](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-meeting?u=76281980&t=69)** Because otherwise, people accept the first meeting and then they get an update for each one of the ones I change.
>
> **[1:15](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-meeting?u=76281980&t=75)** So with that exception in mind, I'm going to add our folks to this meeting, Reggie, Rob, Griffin and Simon.
>
> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-meeting?u=76281980&t=92)** So it says no suggested times. That's okay.
>
> **[1:38](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-meeting?u=76281980&t=98)** And it's reminding me that some of these folks are in a different time zone.
>
> **[1:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-meeting?u=76281980&t=101)** I'm going to slide that to 11 and see if that's going to float.
>
> **[1:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-meeting?u=76281980&t=106)** So it occurs every third Tuesday until December 31st, 2024.
>
> **[1:50](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-meeting?u=76281980&t=110)** It's a Microsoft Teams meeting, and I'm going to send this out.
>
> **[1:57](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-meeting?u=76281980&t=117)** So if I now look at my monthly calendar, here's the third Tuesday in February, third Tuesday in March, third Tuesday in April, and so on.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-meeting?u=76281980&t=128)** If I need to change one of these meetings, for example, sliding it by a day, I'm asked to edit.

>
> **[2:24](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-meeting?u=76281980&t=144)** Whereas if I had made those changes ahead of time and I invited them to the series, they would've gotten my series with this exception in it.
>
> **[2:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-meeting?u=76281980&t=152)** If I go back and change the recurrence pattern of this meeting, any that are out of sequence will snap back to the original.
>
> **[2:41](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-meeting?u=76281980&t=161)** So if I simply decided that we were going to change the time by a half an hour, and I needed to edit this, in doing that, any meetings that aren't already on the third Tuesday would come back to the third Tuesday.
>
> **[3:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-meeting?u=76281980&t=180)** This is a great function, but you need to wrestle with it a little bit.
>

>
> **[3:12](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-a-repeating-meeting?u=76281980&t=192)** Set them up as individual meetings.

#### Create and use contact lists

> **[0:00](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-and-use-contact-lists?u=76281980&t=0)** - [Instructor] A contact list originally was a group of people that you wanted to send an email to at the same time.
>
> **[0:06](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-and-use-contact-lists?u=76281980&t=6)** So this is our list of current vendors.

>
> **[0:17](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-and-use-contact-lists?u=76281980&t=17)** These originally were called distribution lists because they were made for distributing email.
>

>

> **[1:32](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-and-share-task-lists?u=76281980&t=92)** If I flag something for today, then its due date is today.

> **[1:36](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-and-share-task-lists?u=76281980&t=96)** If I flag it to tomorrow, it's tomorrow.

>

>
> **[1:54](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-and-share-task-lists?u=76281980&t=114)** Anytime you flag an email in Outlook and choose a particular duration, today, tomorrow, this week, next week, it will automatically end up on the Planned list.
>
> **[2:03](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-and-share-task-lists?u=76281980&t=123)** But it will also be on the Flagged email list because every flagged email is here.
>
> **[2:08](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-and-share-task-lists?u=76281980&t=128)** And if you want to also say, this is important that I do this, you can mark it as important and it's also on the Important list.
>
> **[2:14](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-and-share-task-lists?u=76281980&t=134)** So one of the things that people sometimes find confusing about To Do is that an item can appear on multiple lists because these are just filtered views of all of the items on your To Do list.
>
> **[2:25](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-and-share-task-lists?u=76281980&t=145)** Tasks are simply tasks.
>
> **[2:28](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-and-share-task-lists?u=76281980&t=148)** And so if you want to type in a task, you can do that right here, you can type in a task anywhere.
>
> **[2:35](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-and-share-task-lists?u=76281980&t=155)** I'm going to make a task to upload docs to Teams, and I actually know what that means.
>
> **[2:44](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-and-share-task-lists?u=76281980&t=164)** I don't need anything more than that.
>
> **[2:46](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-and-share-task-lists?u=76281980&t=166)** And so now I have another task.
>
> **[2:47](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-and-share-task-lists?u=76281980&t=167)** I also have some tasks that I completed already and this is what they look like when they're completed.
>
> **[2:53](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-and-share-task-lists?u=76281980&t=173)** I passed over one item, which is Assigned to me.
>
> **[2:55](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-and-share-task-lists?u=76281980&t=175)** And the way things get on the Assigned to me list is typically through Planner.
>
> **[3:01](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-and-share-task-lists?u=76281980&t=181)** Someone creates a task for you in Planner and that's how it gets assigned to you.
>
> **[3:07](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-and-share-task-lists?u=76281980&t=187)** Now, let's go back to My Day.
>

>
> **[3:23](https://www.linkedin.com/learning/outlook-on-the-web-essential-training-23727889/create-and-share-task-lists?u=76281980&t=203)** New logo replacements, huh, that's cool.
